     <article id="post-1481" class="post-1481 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-gensim category-programming tag-gensim tag-optimization tag-word2vec"> 
      <div class="entry-wrap"> 
       <header class="entry-header"> 
        <h1 class="entry-title">Word2vec Tutorial</h1> 
        <p class="p-meta"><span><a href=" https://rare-technologies.com/author/radim/ "><i class="x-icon-pencil" data-x-icon="?"></i> Radim ?eh??ek</a></span><span><time class="entry-date" datetime="2014-02-02T16:06:35+00:00"><i class="x-icon-calendar" data-x-icon="?"></i> 2014-02-02</time></span><span><a href="https://rare-technologies.com/category/gensim/" title="View all posts in: “gensim”"><i class="x-icon-bookmark" data-x-icon="?"></i> gensim</a>, <a href="https://rare-technologies.com/category/programming/" title="View all posts in: “programming”"><i class="x-icon-bookmark" data-x-icon="?"></i> programming</a></span><span><a href="https://rare-technologies.com/word2vec-tutorial/#comments" title="Leave a comment on: “Word2vec Tutorial”" class="meta-comments"><i class="x-icon-comments" data-x-icon="?"></i> 147 Comments</a></span></p>
       </header> 
       <div class="entry-content content"> 
        <p> I never got round to writing a tutorial on how to use word2vec in gensim. It’s simple enough and the <a href="http://radimrehurek.com/gensim/models/word2vec.html" target="_blank">API docs</a> are straightforward, but I know some people prefer more verbose formats. Let this post be a tutorial and a reference example. </p> 
        <span id="more-1481"></span> 
        <p><strong>UPDATE</strong>: the complete HTTP server code for the interactive word2vec demo below is now <a href="https://github.com/RaRe-Technologies/w2v_server_googlenews">open sourced on github</a>.</p> 
        <h3 id="preparing-input">Preparing the Input</h3> 
        <p> Starting from the beginning, gensim’s word2vec expects a sequence of sentences as its input. Each sentence a list of words (utf8 strings): </p> 
        <pre class="brush: python; title: ; notranslate" title=""># import modules &amp; set up logging
import gensim, logging
logging.basicConfig(format='%(asctime)s : %(levelname)s : %(message)s', level=logging.INFO)

sentences = [['first', 'sentence'], ['second', 'sentence']]
# train word2vec on the two sentences
model = gensim.models.Word2Vec(sentences, min_count=1)
</pre> 
        <p> Keeping the input as a Python built-in list is convenient, but can use up a lot of RAM when the input is large. </p> 
        <p> Gensim only requires that the input must provide sentences <em>sequentially</em>, when iterated over. No need to keep everything in RAM: we can provide one sentence, process it, forget it, load another sentence… </p> 
        <p> For example, if our input is strewn across several files on disk, with one sentence per line, then instead of loading everything into an in-memory list, we can process the input file by file, line by line: </p> 
        <pre class="brush: python; title: ; notranslate" title="">class MySentences(object):
    def __init__(self, dirname):
        self.dirname = dirname

    def __iter__(self):
        for fname in os.listdir(self.dirname):
            for line in open(os.path.join(self.dirname, fname)):
                yield line.split()

sentences = MySentences('/some/directory') # a memory-friendly iterator
model = gensim.models.Word2Vec(sentences)
</pre> 
        <p> Say we want to further preprocess the words from the files — convert to unicode, lowercase, remove numbers, extract named entities… All of this can be done inside the MySentences iterator and word2vec doesn’t need to know. All that is required is that the input yields one sentence (list of utf8 words) after another. </p> 
        <p> <strong>Note to advanced users</strong>: calling <em>Word2Vec(sentences, iter=1)</em> will run two passes over the sentences iterator (or, in general <em>iter+1</em> passes; default <em>iter=5</em>). The first pass collects words and their frequencies to build an internal dictionary tree structure. The second and subsequent passes train the neural model. These two (or, <em>iter+1</em>) passes can also be initiated manually, in case your input stream is non-repeatable (you can only afford one pass), and you’re able to initialize the vocabulary some other way: </p> 
        <pre class="brush: python; title: ; notranslate" title="">model = gensim.models.Word2Vec(iter=1)  # an empty model, no training yet
model.build_vocab(some_sentences)  # can be a non-repeatable, 1-pass generator
model.train(other_sentences)  # can be a non-repeatable, 1-pass generator
</pre> 
        <p> In case you’re confused about iterators, iterables and generators in Python, check out our tutorial on <a href="https://rare-technologies.com/data-streaming-in-python-generators-iterators-iterables/">Data Streaming in Python</a>. </p> 
        <h3 id="training">Training</h3> 
        <p> Word2vec accepts several parameters that affect both training speed and quality. </p> 
        <p> One of them is for pruning the internal dictionary. Words that appear only once or twice in a billion-word corpus are probably uninteresting typos and garbage. In addition, there’s not enough data to make any meaningful training on those words, so it’s best to ignore them: </p> 
        <pre class="brush: python; title: ; notranslate" title="">model = Word2Vec(sentences, min_count=10)  # default value is 5
</pre> 
        <p> A reasonable value for <em>min_count</em> is between 0-100, depending on the size of your dataset. </p> 
        <p> Another parameter is the size of the NN layers, which correspond to the “degrees” of freedom the training algorithm has: </p> 
        <pre class="brush: python; title: ; notranslate" title="">model = Word2Vec(sentences, size=200)  # default value is 100
</pre> 
        <p> Bigger <em>size</em> values require more training data, but can lead to better (more accurate) models. Reasonable values are in the tens to hundreds. </p> 
        <p> The last of the major parameters (full list <a href="http://radimrehurek.com/gensim/models/word2vec.html#gensim.models.word2vec.Word2Vec" target="_blank">here</a>) is for training parallelization, to speed up training: </p> 
        <pre class="brush: python; title: ; notranslate" title="">model = Word2Vec(sentences, workers=4) # default = 1 worker = no parallelization
</pre> 
        <p> The <em>workers</em> parameter has only effect if you have <a href="http://cython.org/" target="_blank">Cython</a> installed. Without Cython, you’ll only be able to use one core because of the <a href="https://wiki.python.org/moin/GlobalInterpreterLock" target="_blank">GIL</a> (and word2vec training will be <a href="http://radimrehurek.com/2013/09/word2vec-in-python-part-two-optimizing/" target="_blank">miserably slow</a>). </p> 
        <script type="text/javascript">(function() {
	if (!window.mc4wp) {
		window.mc4wp = {
			listeners: [],
			forms    : {
				on: function (event, callback) {
					window.mc4wp.listeners.push({
						event   : event,
						callback: callback
					});
				}
			}
		}
	}
})();
</script>
        <form id="mc4wp-form-1" class="mc4wp-form mc4wp-form-7254" method="post" data-id="7254" data-name="Form">
         <div class="mc4wp-form-fields">
          <div style="border: 1px solid; border-radius: 6px; border-color: #D7AD7C; padding: 25px;"> 
           <p> <em>Note from Radim: Get my latest machine learning tips &amp; articles delivered straight to your inbox (it's free).</em> </p> 
           <span> <input type="text" name="FNAME" placeholder="Your first name" style="border-radius:5px; -moz-border-radius:5px; -webkit-border-radius:5px; width: 25%; display: inline-block;"> <input type="email" id="mc4wp_email" name="EMAIL" placeholder="Your email address" style="border-radius:5px; -moz-border-radius:5px; -webkit-border-radius:5px; width: 65%; display: inline-block;"> </span>

          </div>
          <div style="display: none;">

        </form> 
        <h3 id="memory">Memory</h3> 
        <p> At its core, word2vec model parameters are stored as matrices (NumPy arrays). Each array is <strong>#vocabulary</strong> (controlled by <em>min_count</em> parameter) times <strong>#size</strong> (<em>size</em> parameter) of <strong>floats</strong> (single precision aka 4 bytes). </p> 
        <p> Three such matrices are held in RAM (work is underway to reduce that number to two, or even one). So if your input contains 100,000 unique words, and you asked for layer size=200, the model will require approx. 100,000*200*4*3 bytes = ~229MB. </p> 
        <p> There’s a little extra memory needed for storing the vocabulary tree (100,000 words would take a few megabytes), but unless your words are extremely loooong strings, memory footprint will be dominated by the three matrices above. </p> 
        <h3 id="evaluating">Evaluating</h3> 
        <p> Word2vec training is an unsupervised task, there’s no good way to objectively evaluate the result. Evaluation depends on your end application. </p> 
        <p> Google have released their testing set of about 20,000 syntactic and semantic test examples, following the “A is to B as C is to D” task: <a href="https://word2vec.googlecode.com/svn/trunk/questions-words.txt" target="_blank">http://word2vec.googlecode.com/svn/trunk/questions-words.txt</a>. </p> 
        <p> Gensim support the same evaluation set, in exactly the same format: </p> 
        <pre class="brush: python; title: ; notranslate" title="">model.accuracy('/tmp/questions-words.txt')
2014-02-01 22:14:28,387 : INFO : family: 88.9% (304/342)
2014-02-01 22:29:24,006 : INFO : gram1-adjective-to-adverb: 32.4% (263/812)
2014-02-01 22:36:26,528 : INFO : gram2-opposite: 50.3% (191/380)
2014-02-01 23:00:52,406 : INFO : gram3-comparative: 91.7% (1222/1332)
2014-02-01 23:13:48,243 : INFO : gram4-superlative: 87.9% (617/702)
2014-02-01 23:29:52,268 : INFO : gram5-present-participle: 79.4% (691/870)
2014-02-01 23:57:04,965 : INFO : gram7-past-tense: 67.1% (995/1482)
2014-02-02 00:15:18,525 : INFO : gram8-plural: 89.6% (889/992)
2014-02-02 00:28:18,140 : INFO : gram9-plural-verbs: 68.7% (482/702)
2014-02-02 00:28:18,140 : INFO : total: 74.3% (5654/7614)
</pre> 
        <p> This <em>accuracy</em> takes an <a href="http://radimrehurek.com/gensim/models/word2vec.html#gensim.models.word2vec.Word2Vec.accuracy" target="_blank">optional parameter</a> <em>restrict_vocab</em> which limits which test examples are to be considered. </p> 
        <p> Once again, <strong>good performance on this test set doesn’t mean word2vec will work well in your application, or vice versa</strong>. It’s always best to evaluate directly on your intended task. </p> 
        <h3 id="persistence">Storing and loading models</h3> 
        <p> You can store/load models using the standard gensim methods: </p> 
        <pre class="brush: python; title: ; notranslate" title="">model.save('/tmp/mymodel')
new_model = gensim.models.Word2Vec.load('/tmp/mymodel')
</pre> 
        <p> which uses pickle internally, optionally <em>mmap</em>‘ing the model’s internal large NumPy matrices into virtual memory directly from disk files, for inter-process memory sharing. </p> 
        <p> In addition, you can load models created by the original C tool, both using its text and binary formats: </p> 
        <pre class="brush: python; title: ; notranslate" title="">model = Word2Vec.load_word2vec_format('/tmp/vectors.txt', binary=False)
# using gzipped/bz2 input works too, no need to unzip:
model = Word2Vec.load_word2vec_format('/tmp/vectors.bin.gz', binary=True)
</pre> 
        <h3 id="resuming">Online training / Resuming training</h3> 
        <p> Advanced users can load a model and continue training it with more sentences: </p> 
        <pre class="brush: python; title: ; notranslate" title="">model = gensim.models.Word2Vec.load('/tmp/mymodel')
model.train(more_sentences)
</pre> 
        <p> You may need to tweak the <em>total_words</em> parameter to <em>train()</em>, depending on what learning rate decay you want to simulate. </p> 
        <p> Note that it’s not possible to resume training with models generated by the C tool, <em>load_word2vec_format()</em>. You can still use them for querying/similarity, but information vital for training (the vocab tree) is missing there. </p> 
        <h3 id="using">Using the model</h3> 
        <p> Word2vec supports several word similarity tasks out of the box: </p> 
        <pre class="brush: python; title: ; notranslate" title="">model.most_similar(positive=['woman', 'king'], negative=['man'], topn=1)
[('queen', 0.50882536)]
model.doesnt_match("breakfast cereal dinner lunch";.split())
'cereal'
model.similarity('woman', 'man')
0.73723527
</pre> 
        <p> If you need the raw output vectors in your application, you can access these either on a word-by-word basis </p> 
        <pre class="brush: python; title: ; notranslate" title="">model['computer']  # raw NumPy vector of a word
array([-0.00449447, -0.00310097,  0.02421786, ...], dtype=float32)
</pre> 
        <p> …or en-masse as a 2D NumPy matrix from <em>model.syn0</em>. </p> 
        <h3 id="app">Bonus app</h3> 
        <p> As before with <a href="http://radimrehurek.com/2014/01/performance-shootout-of-nearest-neighbours-querying/#wikisim" target="_blank">finding similar articles in the English Wikipedia with Latent Semantic Analysis</a>, here’s a bonus web app for those who managed to read this far. It uses the word2vec model trained by Google on the Google News dataset, on <strong>about 100 billion words</strong>: </p> 
        <link rel="stylesheet" type="text/css" href="//ajax.googleapis.com/ajax/libs/jqueryui/1/themes/smoothness/jquery-ui.css"> 
        <script type="text/javascript" src="//ajax.googleapis.com/ajax/libs/jqueryui/1/jquery-ui.min.js"></script> 
        <style>
    .phrase_autocomplete {
        display: inline-block !important;
    }
    </style> 
        <div style="border: 1px solid; border-radius: 6px; border-color: #D7AD7C; padding: 25px;"> 
         <div> 
          <span id="timing" style="font-size: 0.8em; font-weight: bold;"></span> 
          <span id="details" style="font-size: 0.8em;"></span> 
         </div> 
         <hr> 
         <p> </p>
         <p style="font-size: 0.8em;"> If you don’t get “queen” back, something went wrong and baby SkyNet cries.<br> Try more examples too: <a href="#" id="heshe">“he” is to “his” as “she” is to ?</a>, <a href="#" id="berlinparis">“Berlin” is to “Germany” as “Paris” is to ?</a> (click to fill in). </p> 
         <input placeholder="" value="man" id="phrase_a" type="text" size="18" class="phrase_autocomplete"> is to 
         <input placeholder="" value="king" id="phrase_b" type="text" size="18" class="phrase_autocomplete"> as 
         <input placeholder="" value="woman" id="phrase_c" type="text" size="18" class="phrase_autocomplete"> is to 
         <button id="isto" class="demo-button button" disabled> <span id="result_isto">?</span> </button> 
         <p></p> 
         <hr> 
         <p> </p>
         <p style="font-size: 0.8em;"> Try: <a href="#" id="ny">U.S.A.</a>; <a href="#" id="obama">Monty_Python</a>; <a href="#" id="php">PHP</a>; <a href="#" id="mandela">Madiba</a> (click to fill in). </p> 
         <input placeholder="" value="iPhone" id="phrase_single" type="text" size="40" class="phrase_autocomplete"> 
         <button id="single" class="demo-button button" disabled> <span id="result_single">Get most similar</span> </button> 
         <p></p> 
         <hr> 
         <p> </p>
         <p style="font-size: 0.8em;"> Also try: <a href="#" id="monkeys">“monkey ape baboon human chimp gorilla”</a>; <a href="#" id="colours">“blue red green crimson transparent”</a> (click to fill in). </p> 
         <input placeholder="" value="dinner cereal breakfast lunch" id="phrase_nofit" type="text" size="70"> 
         <button id="nofit" class="demo-button button" disabled> <span id="result_nofit">Which phrase doesn’t fit?</span> </button> 
         <p></p> 
         <hr> 
        </div> 
        <script>
    jQuery(document).ready(function ($) {
        $('.phrase_autocomplete').autocomplete({
            source: 'https://h2.rare-technologies.com/w2v/suggest',
            delay: 100,
            autoFocus: true
        });
        $('#phrase_a, #phrase_b, #phrase_c').focus(function() {
            $('#result_isto').html('?');
        });
        $('#phrase_single').focus(function() {
            $('#result_single').html('Get most similar');
        });
        $('#phrase_nofit').focus(function() {
            $('#result_nofit').html("Which phrase doesn't fit?");
        });
        $('#heshe').click(function() {
            $('#phrase_a').val("he");
            $('#phrase_b').val("his");
            $('#phrase_c').val("she").focus();
            return false;
        });
        $('#berlinparis').click(function() {
            $('#phrase_a').val("Berlin");
            $('#phrase_b').val("Germany");
            $('#phrase_c').val("Paris").focus();
            return false;
        });
        $('#ny').click(function() {
            $('#phrase_single').val("U.S.A.").focus();
            return false;
        });
        $('#obama').click(function() {
            $('#phrase_single').val("Monty_Python").focus();
            return false;
        });
        $('#php').click(function() {
            $('#phrase_single').val("PHP").focus();
            return false;
        });
        $('#mandela').click(function() {
            $('#phrase_single').val("Madiba").focus();
            return false;
        });
        $('#monkeys').click(function() {
            $('#phrase_nofit').val("monkey ape baboon human chimp gorilla").focus();
            return false;
        });
        $('#colours').click(function() {
            $('#phrase_nofit').val("blue red green crimson transparent").focus();
            return false;
        });
        $('#isto').click(function() {
            var data = {
                'positive': [$('#phrase_c').val(), $('#phrase_b').val()],
                'negative': [$('#phrase_a').val()]
            };

            $.get('https://h2.rare-technologies.com/w2v/most_similar', data, function(data) {
                var result = data.similars.length > 0 ? data.similars[0][0] : '';
                $('#result_isto').html(result);
                $('#details').html(JSON.stringify(data.similars));
                $('#timing').html(Math.round(10000 * data.taken) / 10 + "ms");
            });
        });
        $('#single').click(function() {
            var data = {
                'positive': [$('#phrase_single').val()]
            };

            $.get('https://h2.rare-technologies.com/w2v/most_similar', data, function(data) {
                var result = data.similars.length > 0 ? data.similars[0][0] : '';
                $('#result_single').html(result);
                $('#details').html(JSON.stringify(data.similars));
                $('#timing').html(Math.round(10000 * data.taken) / 10 + "ms");
            });
        });
        $('#nofit').click(function() {
            var data = {
                'words': [$('#phrase_nofit').val()]
            };

            $.get('https://h2.rare-technologies.com/w2v/most_dissimilar', data, function(data) {
                var result = data.dissimilar ? data.dissimilar : '';
                $('#result_nofit').html(result);
                $('#details').html('');
                $('#timing').html(Math.round(10000 * data.taken) / 10 + "ms");
            });
        });
        $('.demo-button').prop("disabled", false);
    });
    </script> 
        <br> 
        <p> The model contains <strong>3,000,000 unique phrases</strong> built with <strong>layer size of 300</strong>. </p> 
        <p> Note that the similarities were trained on a news dataset, and that Google did very little preprocessing there. So the phrases are <strong>case sensitive: watch out</strong>! Especially with proper nouns. </p> 
        <p> On a related note, I noticed about half the queries people entered into the <a href="http://radimrehurek.com/2014/01/performance-shootout-of-nearest-neighbours-querying/#wikisim" target="_blank"><span class="__cf_email__" data-cfemail="e7abb4a6a7b08e8c8e">[email&nbsp;protected]</span> demo</a> contained typos/spelling errors, so they found nothing. Ouch. </p> 
        <p> To make it a little less challenging this time, I added <strong>phrase suggestions</strong> to the forms above. Start typing to see a list of valid phrases from the actual vocabulary of Google News’ word2vec model. </p> 
        <p> The “suggested” phrases are simply ten phrases starting from whatever <em>bisect_left(all_model_phrases_alphabetically_sorted, prefix_you_typed_so_far)</em> from Python’s built-in <a href="https://docs.python.org/2/library/bisect.html" target="_blank">bisect module</a> returns. </p> 
        <p> See the complete HTTP server code for this “bonus app” <a href="https://github.com/RaRe-Technologies/w2v_server_googlenews">on github</a> (using CherryPy). </p> 
        <h3 id="outro">Outro</h3> 
        <p> Full word2vec API docs <a href="http://radimrehurek.com/gensim/models/word2vec.html" target="_blank">here</a>; get gensim <a href="http://radimrehurek.com/gensim/" target="_blank">here</a>. Original C toolkit and word2vec papers by Google <a href="https://code.google.com/p/word2vec/" target="_blank">here</a>. </p> 
        <p> And here’s me talking about the optimizations behind word2vec at <a href="http://pydata.org/berlin2014/">PyData Berlin 2014</a> <iframe width="742" height="417" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/vU4TlwZzTfU?feature=oembed" frameborder="0" allowfullscreen></iframe> </p> 
       </div> 
      </div>

         <section class="x-comment-content"> 
          <p>Hi Radim,</p> 
          <p> Is there any way to obtain the similarity of phrases out of the word2vec? I’m trying to get 2-word phrases to compare, but don’t know how to do it.</p> 
          <p>Thanks!<br> Pavel</p> 
         </section> 
         <div class="x-reply"> 
          <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://rare-technologies.com/word2vec-tutorial/?replytocom=2262#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-2262&quot;, &quot;2262&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;1481&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Pavel">Reply <input type="hidden" id="id_replay_for_comment" value="2262"> <span class="comment-reply-link-after"><i class="x-icon-reply" data-x-icon="?"></i></span></a>

        <ol class="children"> 
         <li id="li-comment-2265" class="comment byuser comment-author-radim bypostauthor even depth-2"> 
          <div class="x-comment-img">
           <span class="avatar-wrap cf"><img src="//rare-technologies.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/04/radim.jpg" width="120" height="94" alt="Radim" class="avatar avatar-120 wp-user-avatar wp-user-avatar-120 alignnone photo"></span> 
           <span class="bypostauthor">Post<br>Author</span>
          </div> 
          <article id="comment-2265" class="comment"> 
           <header class="x-comment-header"> 
            <cite class="x-comment-author">Radim</cite>
            <div>
             <a href="https://rare-technologies.com/word2vec-tutorial/#comment-2265" class="x-comment-time"><time datetime="2014-04-06T13:17:58+00:00">2014-04-06 at 1:17 pm</time></a>
            </div> 
           </header> 
           <section class="x-comment-content"> 
            <p>Hello Pavel, yes, there is a way.</p> 
            <p>First, you must detect phrases in the text (such as 2-word phrases).</p> 
            <p>Then you build the word2vec model like you normally would, except some “tokens” will be strings of multiple words instead of one (example sentence: [“New York”, “was”, “founded”, “16th century”]).</p> 
            <p>Then, to get similarity of phrases, you do `model.similarity(“New York”, “16th century”)`.</p> 
            <p>It may be a good idea to replace spaces with underscores in the phrase-tokens, to avoid potential parsing problems (“New_York”, “16th_century”).</p> 
            <p>As for detecting the phrases, it’s a task unrelated to word2vec. You can use existing NLP tools like the NLTK/Freebase, or help finish a gensim pull request that does exactly this: <a href="https://github.com/piskvorky/gensim/pull/135" rel="nofollow">https://github.com/piskvorky/gensim/pull/135</a> .</p> 
           </section>

            <p>Hello Max, </p> 
            <p>thanks ?</p> 
            <p>Skip-gram is used because it gives better (more accurate) results.</p> 
            <p>CBOW is faster though. If you have lots data, you can be advantageous to run the simpler but faster model.</p> 
            <p>There’s a <a href="https://github.com/piskvorky/gensim/pull/162" rel="nofollow">pull request under way</a>, to enable all the word2vec options and parameters. You can try out the various models and their performance for yourself ?</p>

            </div> 
           </header> 
           <section class="x-comment-content"> 
            <p>Hi, it can be done directly for languages where you can split text into sentences and tokens.</p> 
            <p>The only concern would be that the `window` parameter has to be large enough to capture syntactic/semantic relationships. For English, the default `window=5`, and I wouldn’t expect it to be dramatically different for other languages.</p>

       <li id="li-comment-2279" class="comment even thread-even depth-1"> 
        <div class="x-comment-img">
         <span class="avatar-wrap cf"><img src="//secure.gravatar.com/avatar/3f4afac62281765f73e21950d589ad77?s=120&amp;r=g" width="120" height="120" alt="" class="avatar avatar-120wp-user-avatar wp-user-avatar-120 alignnone photo avatar-default"></span> 
        </div> 
        <article id="comment-2279" class="comment"> 
         <header class="x-comment-header"> 
          <cite class="x-comment-author">Zigi</cite>
          <div>
           <a href="https://rare-technologies.com/word2vec-tutorial/#comment-2279" class="x-comment-time"><time datetime="2014-06-13T04:36:30+00:00">2014-06-13 at 4:36 am</time></a>
          </div> 
         </header> 
         <section class="x-comment-content"> 
          <p>Hi,<br> could you please explain how do CBOW and skip-gram models actually do the learning. I’ve read ‘Efficient estimation…’ but it doesn’t really explain how does the actual training happen.<br> I’ve taken a look at the original source code and your implementation, and while I can understand the code I cannot understand the logic behind it. </p> 
          <p>I don’t understand these lines in your implementation (word2vec.py, gensim 0.9) CBOW:<br> ————————————<br> l2a = model.syn1[word.point] # 2d matrix, codelen x layer1_size<br> fa = 1.0 / (1.0 + exp(-dot(l1, l2a.T))) # propagate hidden -&gt; output<br> ga = (1 – word.code – fa) * alpha # vector of error gradients multiplied by the learning rate<br> model.syn1[word.point] += outer(ga, l1) # learn hidden -&gt; output<br> —————————————-<br> I see that it has something to do with the Huffman-tree word representation, but despite the comments, I don’t understand what is actually happening, what does syn1 represent, why do we multiply l1 with l2a… why are we multiplying ga and l1 etc…</p> 
          <p>Could you please explain in a sentence or two what is actually happening in there.<br> I would be very grateful.</p> 
         </section>

           <section class="x-comment-content"> 
            <p>The weights are a NumPy matrix — have a look at `model.syn0` and `model.syn1` matrices. You can append new vectors easily.</p> 
            <p>Off the top of my head I’m not sure whether there are any other variables in `model` that need to be modified when you do this. There probably are. I’d suggest checking the code to make sure everything’s consistent.</p>

            <div>
             <a href="https://rare-technologies.com/word2vec-tutorial/#comment-2285" class="x-comment-time"><time datetime="2014-08-21T17:07:14+00:00">2014-08-21 at 5:07 pm</time></a>
            </div> 
           </header> 
           <section class="x-comment-content"> 
            <p>Good questions, but I don’t have any insights beyond the standard advice:</p> 
            <p>1. unknown words are ignored; or you can build a model with one special “word” to represent all OOV words.</p> 
            <p>2. for short sentences/phrases, you can average the individual vectors; for longer texts, look into something like paragraph2vec: <a href="https://github.com/piskvorky/gensim/issues/204#issuecomment-52093328" rel="nofollow">https://github.com/piskvorky/gensim/issues/204#issuecomment-52093328</a></p> 
           </section>

            </div> 
           </header> 
           <section class="x-comment-content"> 
            <p>It parallelizes training.</p> 
            <p>How you iterate over sentences is your business — word2vec only expects an iterator on input. What the iterator does internally to iterate over sentences is up to you and not part of word2vec.</p> 
           </section>

                 <a href="https://rare-technologies.com/word2vec-tutorial/#comment-2307" class="x-comment-time"><time datetime="2015-03-18T16:41:40+00:00">2015-03-18 at 4:41 pm</time></a>
                </div> 
               </header> 
               <section class="x-comment-content"> 
                <p>Oh, non-ASCII characters.</p> 
                <p>IIRC, the C code doesn’t handle unicode in any way, all text is treated as binary. Python code (gensim) uses Unicode for strings.</p> 
                <p>So, perhaps some encoding mismatch?</p> 
                <p>How was your model trained — with C code? Is so, what was the encoding?</p>

              <p>from gensim.models import word2vec<br> model_path = “…/GoogleNews-vectors-negative300.bin”<br> model = word2vec.Word2Vec.load_word2vec_format(model_path, binary=True)<br> stringA = ‘woman’<br> stringB = ‘king’<br> stringC = ‘man’<br> print model.most_similar(positive=[stringA, stringB], negative=[stringC], topn=10)</p>

         <section class="x-comment-content"> 
          <p>Hi Radim,</p> 
          <p>Thanks for such a nice package! It may be bold to suggest, but I ran across what I think might be a bug. It’s likely a features :), but I thought I’d point it out since I needed to fix it in an unintuitive way.</p> 
          <p>If I train a word2vec model using a list of sentences:</p> 
          <p>sentences = MySentences(fname) # generator that yields sentences<br> mysentences = list(sentences)<br> model = gensim.models.Word2Vec(sentences=mysentences **kwargs)</p> 
          <p>then the model finishes training. Eg., the end of the logging shows</p> 
          <p>…snip…<br> 2015-05-13 22:12:07,329 : INFO : PROGRESS: at 97.17% words, alpha 0.00075, 47620 words/s<br> 2015-05-13 22:12:08,359 : INFO : PROGRESS: at 98.25% words, alpha 0.00049, 47605 words/s<br> 2015-05-13 22:12:09,362 : INFO : PROGRESS: at 99.32% words, alpha 0.00019, 47603 words/s<br> 2015-05-13 22:12:09,519 : INFO : reached the end of input; waiting to finish 16 outstanding jobs<br> 2015-05-13 22:12:09,901 : INFO : training on 4427131 words took 92.9s, 47648 words/s</p> 
          <p>I’m training on many GB of data, so I need to pass in a generator that yields sentences line by line (like your MySentences class above). But when I try it as suggested with, say, iter=5:</p> 
          <p>sentences = MySentences(fname) # generator that yields sentences<br> model = gensim.models.Word2Vec(sentences=None, **kwargs) # iter=10 defined in kwargs<br> ?model.build_vocab(sentences_vocab)?<br> model.train(sentences_train)</p> 
          <p>the model stops training 1/20 of the way through. If iter=10, it stops 1/10 of the way, etc. Eg., the end of the logging looks like,</p> 
          <p>…snip…<br> 2015-05-13 22:31:37,265 : INFO : PROGRESS: at 18.21% words, alpha 0.02049, 49695 words/s<br> 2015-05-13 22:31:38,266 : INFO : PROGRESS: at 19.29% words, alpha 0.02022, 49585 words/s<br> 2015-05-13 22:31:38,452 : INFO : reached the end of input; waiting to finish 16 outstanding jobs<br> 2015-05-13 22:31:38,857 : INFO : training on 885538 words took 17.8s, 49703 words/s</p> 
          <p>Looking in word2vec.py, around line 316 I noticed </p> 
          <p>sentences = gensim.utils.RepeatCorpusNTimes(sentences, iter)</p> 
          <p>so I added </p> 
          <p>sentences_train = gensim.utils.RepeatCorpusNTimes(Sentences(fname), model.iter)</p> 
          <p>before calling model.train() in the above code snippet. Does this seem like the correct course of action, or am I missing something fundamental about the way one should stream sentences to build the vocab and train the model? </p> 
          <p>Thanks for your help,<br> Jesse</p>

         <li id="li-comment-2319" class="comment byuser comment-author-radim bypostauthor even depth-2"> 
          <div class="x-comment-img">
           <span class="avatar-wrap cf"><img src="//rare-technologies.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/04/radim.jpg" width="120" height="94" alt="Radim" class="avatar avatar-120 wp-user-avatar wp-user-avatar-120 alignnone photo"></span> 
           <span class="bypostauthor">Post<br>Author</span>
          </div> 
          <article id="comment-2319" class="comment"> 
           <header class="x-comment-header"> 
            <cite class="x-comment-author"><a href="http://radimrehurek.com" rel="external nofollow" class="url">Radim</a></cite>
            <div>
             <a href="https://rare-technologies.com/word2vec-tutorial/#comment-2319" class="x-comment-time"><time datetime="2015-05-14T09:38:38+00:00">2015-05-14 at 9:38 am</time></a>
            </div> 
           </header> 
           <section class="x-comment-content"> 
            <p>Hello Jesse,</p> 
            <p>for your sentences, are you using a generator (=can be iterated over only once), or an iterable (can be iterated over many times)?</p> 
            <p>It is true that for multiple passes, generator is not enough. Anyway better ask at the gensim mailing list / github, that’s a better medium for this:<br> <a href="http://radimrehurek.com/gensim/support.html" rel="nofollow">http://radimrehurek.com/gensim/support.html</a></p> 
           </section>

       <li id="li-comment-2332" class="comment odd alt thread-even depth-1"> 
        <div class="x-comment-img">
         <span class="avatar-wrap cf"><img src="//secure.gravatar.com/avatar/1958946b318142febf55758b3e867bf1?s=120&amp;r=g" width="120" height="120" alt="" class="avatar avatar-120wp-user-avatar wp-user-avatar-120 alignnone photo avatar-default"></span>

        <article id="comment-2332" class="comment"> 
         <header class="x-comment-header"> 
          <cite class="x-comment-author">Mike</cite>
          <div>
           <a href="https://rare-technologies.com/word2vec-tutorial/#comment-2332" class="x-comment-time"><time datetime="2015-08-10T19:07:54+00:00">2015-08-10 at 7:07 pm</time></a>
          </div> 
         </header> 
         <section class="x-comment-content"> 
          <p>Ok…I was able to make a couple changes to word2vec.py to get it to run on my computer:</p> 
          <p>The current version uses numpy.uint32 on lines 83, 327, 373, and 522. This was causing an overflow error when converting to C long. </p> 
          <p>I changed these to reference numpy.uint64 and it *almost* worked….the use of uint64 on line 522 for setting the seed of the random number generator resulted in a seed value being out of bounds. I addressed this by truncating the seed to the max allowable seed:</p> 
          <p>“random.seed(min(uint64(self.hashfxn(self.index2word[i] + str(self.seed))),4294967295))”</p> 
          <p>now everything runs fine (except that my version is not compiled under C so I may see some performance issues for large coropra)…</p> 
         </section> 
         <div class="x-reply"> 
          <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://rare-technologies.com/word2vec-tutorial/?replytocom=2332#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-2332&quot;, &quot;2332&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;1481&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Mike">Reply <input type="hidden" id="id_replay_for_comment" value="2332"> <span class="comment-reply-link-after"><i class="x-icon-reply" data-x-icon="?"></i></span></a>

       <li id="li-comment-2333" class="comment even thread-odd thread-alt depth-1"> 
        <div class="x-comment-img">
         <span class="avatar-wrap cf"><img src="//secure.gravatar.com/avatar/1958946b318142febf55758b3e867bf1?s=120&amp;r=g" width="120" height="120" alt="" class="avatar avatar-120wp-user-avatar wp-user-avatar-120 alignnone photo avatar-default"></span> 
        </div> 
        <article id="comment-2333" class="comment"> 
         <header class="x-comment-header"> 
          <cite class="x-comment-author">Mike</cite>
          <div>
           <a href="https://rare-technologies.com/word2vec-tutorial/#comment-2333" class="x-comment-time"><time datetime="2015-08-10T20:49:19+00:00">2015-08-10 at 8:49 pm</time></a>
          </div> 
         </header> 
         <section class="x-comment-content"> 
          <p>actually, there is a solution on Kaggle for 64-bit machines that worked really well (do not use my solution…it results in all word vectors being collinear).</p> 
          <p>def hash32(value):<br> return hash(value) &amp; 0xffffffff</p> 
          <p>Then pass the following arugument to Word2Vec: hashfxn=hash32</p> 
          <p>This will overwrite the base hashfxn and resolve the issues. Also, all my cosine similarities were not 1 now!!</p> 
         </section> 
         <div class="x-reply"> 
          <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://rare-technologies.com/word2vec-tutorial/?replytocom=2333#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-2333&quot;, &quot;2333&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;1481&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Mike">Reply <input type="hidden" id="id_replay_for_comment" value="2333"> <span class="comment-reply-link-after"><i class="x-icon-reply" data-x-icon="?"></i></span></a>

         <span class="avatar-wrap cf"><img src="//secure.gravatar.com/avatar/f2b9215fa02178194d0cbf2819681824?s=120&amp;r=g" width="120" height="120" alt="" class="avatar avatar-120wp-user-avatar wp-user-avatar-120 alignnone photo avatar-default"></span> 
        </div> 
        <article id="comment-2338" class="comment"> 
         <header class="x-comment-header"> 
          <cite class="x-comment-author">Alexis C</cite>
          <div>
           <a href="https://rare-technologies.com/word2vec-tutorial/#comment-2338" class="x-comment-time"><time datetime="2015-08-13T15:20:19+00:00">2015-08-13 at 3:20 pm</time></a>
          </div> 
         </header> 
         <section class="x-comment-content"> 
          <p>Beware of how you go through your training data :</p> 
          <p>When, in your class “MySentences” you use :<br> “for line in open(os.path.join(self.dirname, fname)): ”</p> 
          <p>As far as I know, it won’t close your file. You’re letting the garbage collector of Python deal with the leak in memory. </p> 
          <p>Use : </p> 
          <p>“with gzip.open(os.path.join(self.dirname, fname)) as f:”</p> 
          <p>instead (Ref : <a href="https://stackoverflow.com/questions/7395542/is-explicitly-closing-files-important" rel="nofollow">http://stackoverflow.com/questions/7395542/is-explicitly-closing-files-important</a> )</p> 
          <p>For training on large dataset, it can be a major bottleneck (it was for me ? ).</p> 
          <p>Thank you very much for your fast implementation of Word2vec and Doc2vec !</p> 
         </section> 
         <div class="x-reply"> 
          <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://rare-technologies.com/word2vec-tutorial/?replytocom=2338#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-2338&quot;, &quot;2338&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;1481&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Alexis C">Reply <input type="hidden" id="id_replay_for_comment" value="2338"> <span class="comment-reply-link-after"><i class="x-icon-reply" data-x-icon="?"></i></span></a>

             <a href="https://rare-technologies.com/word2vec-tutorial/#comment-2339" class="x-comment-time"><time datetime="2015-08-13T16:10:13+00:00">2015-08-13 at 4:10 pm</time></a>
            </div> 
           </header> 
           <section class="x-comment-content"> 
            <p>No, CPython closes the file immediately after the object goes out of scope. There is no leak (though that’s a common misconception and a favourite nitpick).</p> 
            <p>With gzip it makes more sense, but then you should be using <a href="https://github.com/piskvorky/smart_open" rel="nofollow">smart_open</a> anyway (also to work around missing context managers in python 2.6).</p> 
           </section>

          <div class="x-comment-img">
           <span class="avatar-wrap cf"><img src="//rare-technologies.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/04/radim.jpg" width="120" height="94" alt="Radim" class="avatar avatar-120 wp-user-avatar wp-user-avatar-120 alignnone photo"></span> 
          </div> 
          <article id="comment-2343" class="comment"> 
           <header class="x-comment-header"> 
            <cite class="x-comment-author">Radim</cite>
            <div>
             <a href="https://rare-technologies.com/word2vec-tutorial/#comment-2343" class="x-comment-time"><time datetime="2015-09-25T08:24:20+00:00">2015-09-25 at 8:24 am</time></a>
            </div> 
           </header> 
           <section class="x-comment-content"> 
            <p>As far as I know, Google didn’t release their vocabulary/phrase model, nor their text preprocessing method.</p> 
            <p>The only thing you have to go by are the phrases inside the model itself (3 million of them), sorted by frequency.</p> 
            <p>You can lowercase the model vocabulary and match against that, but note that you’ll lose some vectors (no way to tell County_Club from county_club from County_club).</p> 
            <p>You can also try asking at the gensim mailing list, or Tomas Mikolov at his mailing list — better chance someone may have an answer or know something.</p> 
           </section>

             <section class="x-comment-content"> 
              <p>Hi Radim,<br> Thanks for your reply,</p> 
              <p>I went ahead and created a small function which would create bigram and replace the original words if bigram exist in GoogleNews model.</p> 
              <p>and yes, I will join google mailing group.</p> 
              <p>####################################################<br> # bigram creator<br> # try to capture fire_station or Fire_Station rather than using ‘fire’ ‘station’ seperately</p> 
              <p># creating bigram<br> def create_bigram(list):<br> for i in range(0,len(list)-1):<br> #ie. country_club<br> word1 = list[i]+’_’+list[i+1]<br> #ie. Country_club<br> word2 = list[i].capitalize()+’_’+list[i+1]<br> #ie. Country_Clue<br> word3 = list[i].capitalize()+’_’+list[i+1].capitalize()<br> #ie. COUNTRY_CLUE<br> word4 = (list[i]+’_’+list[i+1]).upper()</p> 
              <p> word_list = [word1,word2,word3,word4]</p> 
              <p> for item in word_list:<br> print item<br> if item in model.vocab:<br> list.pop(i)<br> list.pop(i)<br> list.append(item)<br> break</p> 
             </section>

                <cite class="x-comment-author">jin</cite>
                <div>
                 <a href="https://rare-technologies.com/word2vec-tutorial/#comment-2345" class="x-comment-time"><time datetime="2015-09-25T16:08:35+00:00">2015-09-25 at 4:08 pm</time></a>
                </div> 
               </header> 
               <section class="x-comment-content"> 
                <p>here’s fixed code,<br> added a line that will not append new word if len(list) gets shorter</p> 
                <p>####################################################<br> # bigram creator<br> # try to capture fire_station or Fire_Station rather than using ‘fire’ ‘station’ seperately</p> 
                <p># creating bigram<br> def create_bigram(list):<br> for i in range(0,len(list)-1):<br> if i &lt; len(list)-1:<br> #ie. country_club<br> word1 = list[i]+'_'+list[i+1]<br> #ie. Country_club<br> word2 = list[i].capitalize()+'_'+list[i+1]<br> #ie. Country_Clue<br> word3 = list[i].capitalize()+'_'+list[i+1].capitalize()<br> #ie. COUNTRY_CLUE<br> word4 = (list[i]+'_'+list[i+1]).upper()</p> 
                <p> word_list = [word1,word2,word3,word4]</p> 
                <p> for item in word_list:<br> print i<br> if item in model.vocab:<br> list.pop(i)<br> list.pop(i)<br> list.append(item)<br> break</p> 
               </section>

          <p>I have come to a strange behaviour after training; and I wanted to mention it here to you.<br> So when I trained word2vec model, with default parameters (namely the skip-gram model), the results where coherent with what is reported (in this blog and in papers..).<br> When I used the pre-trained “vectors.bin” model from C version of Word2Vec from Tomas, loaded in gensim, everything seems fine as well (notice that the default model of C version is CBOW).<br> Then I tried to train the Gensim Word2Vec with default parameters used in C version (which are: size=200, workers=8, window=8, hs=0, sampling=1e-4, sg=0 (using CBOW), negative=25 and iter=15) and I got a strange “squeezed” or shrank vector representation where most of computed “most_similar” words shared a value of roughly 0.97!! Everything was train on the SAME text8 dataset.<br> So I wondered if you saw such “wrong” training before, with those atypical characteristics (all words in roughly one direction in vector space) and if you know where might be the issue.<br> I am trying different parameters setting to hopefully figure out what is wrong (workers&gt;1? iter?).</p>

            <div>
             <a href="https://rare-technologies.com/word2vec-tutorial/#comment-2356" class="x-comment-time"><time datetime="2015-11-22T11:28:08+00:00">2015-11-22 at 11:28 am</time></a>
            </div> 
           </header> 
           <section class="x-comment-content"> 
            <p>Hello Siva,</p> 
            <p>yes, you have several options there:</p> 
            <p>* <a href="http://radimrehurek.com/gensim/models/word2vec.html#gensim.models.word2vec.Word2Vec.init_sims" rel="nofollow">model.init_sims(replace=True)</a>, to remove unneeded files and save memory, if you don’t want to continue training.<br> * <a href="http://radimrehurek.com/gensim/models/word2vec.html#gensim.models.word2vec.Word2Vec.estimate_memory" rel="nofollow">estimate_memory</a>, to estimate required memory<br> * Look at the log from training, which contains a lot of useful, detailed information and numbers. Always a good idea to store and inspect the log.</p> 
            <p>Hope that helps,<br> Radim</p> 
           </section>

               <section class="x-comment-content"> 
                <p>Hey Rahul,<br> you need to build vocab before training.<br> You need to execute command written in 5th line of “Preparing input” section<br> Example if you have input sentences: [I like ice cream],[I enjoy sleeping]<br> you need to split every word of each sentence<br> sentence = [[‘I’,’like’,’ice’,’cream’],[‘I’,’enjoy’,’sleeping’]]<br> You can split sentences into words by nltk library.<br> I just saw your doubt, thought this will be helpful ?</p>

          <p>Could you help me with this problem ?</p> 
          <p>I use a simple python function load_bin_vec shown as follows to load the Google pretrained .bin model. But I find that the outputs are different from the results using the load_word2vec_format function in gensim.models.Word2Vec.</p> 
          <p>For example:<br> for the word ‘woman’,<br> the vectors loaded by load_bin_vec function return:<br> [ 2.43164062e-01 -7.71484375e-02 -1.03027344e-01 -1.07421875e-01 …]<br> while the vectors loaded by load_word2vec_format function return:<br> [ 9.15656984e-02 -2.90509649e-02 -3.87959108e-02 …]</p> 
          <p>def load_bin_vec(fname):<br> “””<br> Loads 300×1 word vecs from Google (Mikolov) word2vec<br> “””<br> word_vecs = {}<br> with open(fname, “rb”) as f:<br> header = f.readline()<br> vocab_size, layer1_size = map(int, header.split())<br> binary_len = np.dtype(‘float32’).itemsize * layer1_size<br> for line in xrange(vocab_size):<br> word = []<br> while True:<br> ch = f.read(1)<br> if ch == ‘ ‘:<br> word = ”.join(word)<br> break<br> if ch != ‘n’:<br> word.append(ch)<br> word_vecs[word] = np.fromstring(f.read(binary_len), dtype=’float32?)<br> return word_vecs</p>

         <li id="li-comment-2369" class="comment byuser comment-author-radim bypostauthor odd alt depth-2"> 
          <div class="x-comment-img">
           <span class="avatar-wrap cf"><img src="//rare-technologies.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/04/radim.jpg" width="120" height="94" alt="Radim" class="avatar avatar-120 wp-user-avatar wp-user-avatar-120 alignnone photo"></span> 
           <span class="bypostauthor">Post<br>Author</span>
          </div> 
          <article id="comment-2369" class="comment"> 
           <header class="x-comment-header"> 
            <cite class="x-comment-author"><a href="http://radimrehurek.com" rel="external nofollow" class="url">Radim</a></cite>
            <div>
             <a href="https://rare-technologies.com/word2vec-tutorial/#comment-2369" class="x-comment-time"><time datetime="2016-01-11T10:41:13+00:00">2016-01-11 at 10:41 am</time></a>
            </div> 
           </header> 
           <section class="x-comment-content"> 
            <p>Hello sam,</p> 
            <p>you can remove stopwords (any other other words) either as part of your sentences (MySentences in the code above).</p> 
            <p>Or, keep sentences as-is and add a post-filtering step over them:</p> 
            <p>&gt;&gt;&gt; model = gensim.models.Word2Vec()<br> &gt;&gt;&gt; stopword_set = set(…) # your set of words you don’t want<br> &gt;&gt;&gt; discard_stopwords = lambda: ((word for word in sentence if word not in stopword_set) for sentence in sentences)<br> &gt;&gt;&gt; model.build_vocab(discard_stopwords()))<br> &gt;&gt;&gt; model.train(discard_stopwords())</p> 
            <p>In general, questions like this are best posted to the <a href="https://groups.google.com/d/forum/gensim" rel="nofollow">gensim mailing list</a>, so others can benefit from the discussion.</p> 
            <p>Best,<br> Radim</p> 
           </section>

           <section class="x-comment-content"> 
            <p>The 100-billion-word GoogleNews corpus was actually prepared by Google themselves. I don’t think it’s public.</p> 
            <p>Preprocessing: depends on the app. We usually do careful preprocessing; Google didn’t do almost any for the GoogleNews model ? You’ll see it in the word suggestions in the “Bonus App” above. There’s lots of words like “###” and rubbish characters, typos, uppercase variants etc.</p>

                <p>Wikipedia is one example. You can find a script for automatically preprocessing Wikipedia into plain text here: <a href="https://github.com/piskvorky/sim-shootout" rel="nofollow">https://github.com/piskvorky/sim-shootout</a></p>

       <li id="li-comment-2385" class="comment even thread-odd thread-alt depth-1"> 
        <div class="x-comment-img">
         <span class="avatar-wrap cf"><img src="//secure.gravatar.com/avatar/121fd9bdb7409253dface23bbdef342d?s=120&amp;r=g" width="120" height="120" alt="" class="avatar avatar-120wp-user-avatar wp-user-avatar-120 alignnone photo avatar-default"></span> 
        </div> 
        <article id="comment-2385" class="comment"> 
         <header class="x-comment-header"> 
          <cite class="x-comment-author">Heny Chang</cite>
          <div>
           <a href="https://rare-technologies.com/word2vec-tutorial/#comment-2385" class="x-comment-time"><time datetime="2016-04-01T22:03:01+00:00">2016-04-01 at 10:03 pm</time></a>
          </div> 
         </header> 
         <section class="x-comment-content"> 
          <p>Hi Radim,</p> 
          <p>I would like to understand the right way to resume a Word2Vec model and continue the training process. There was no issue that I could save and load the model, and continue training. But, I couldn’t keep the old vocabs built. I used the simple script to test and got confused. Could you help?</p> 
          <p>When I did<br> ===<br> some_sentences = [[‘first’, ‘sentence’], [‘second’, ‘sentence’]]<br> model = Word2Vec(min_count=1)<br> model.build_vocab(some_sentences)<br> model.train(some_sentences)<br> print model.similarity(‘first’,’second’) # no problem<br> other_sentences = [[‘third’, ‘sentence’], [‘fourth’, ‘sentence’]]<br> model.build_vocab(other_sentences)<br> model.train(other_sentences)<br> print model.similarity(‘third’, ‘fourth’) # no problem<br> print model.similarity(‘first’,’second’) # The vocabs in some_sentences are no longer available???<br> ===<br> It complained<br> -0.0450417522552<br> 0.00356975799328<br> Traceback (most recent call last):<br> File “test.py”, line 16, in<br> print model.similarity(‘first’,’second’)<br> File “/usr/local/lib/python2.7/dist-packages/gensim/models/word2vec.py”, line 1233, in similarity<br> return dot(matutils.unitvec(self[w1]), matutils.unitvec(self[w2]))<br> File “/usr/local/lib/python2.7/dist-packages/gensim/models/word2vec.py”, line 1213, in __getitem__<br> return self.syn0[self.vocab[words].index]<br> KeyError: ‘first’<br> ===<br> Furthermore,<br> model = Word2Vec() # an empty model, no training<br> model.build_vocab(some_sentences)<br> model.train(other_sentences)<br> What is this for? After the execution, I can find the similarity between vocabs in some_sentences, but no similarity between vocabs in other_sentences. Vocabs in some_sentences were built but not trained. Vocabs in other_sentences were trained but not built. Do you have a use case to explain me the relationship? I general, we should have all vocabs built and trained first so that we are able to get the relataion between any of them, right? After loading, the old vocabs tree should be there, and allow adding new vocabs to the existing tree and training the new vocabs. Is my understanding correct?</p> 
          <p>Best,<br> Henry</p> 
         </section>

         <li id="li-comment-2386" class="comment byuser comment-author-radim bypostauthor odd alt depth-2"> 
          <div class="x-comment-img">
           <span class="avatar-wrap cf"><img src="//rare-technologies.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/04/radim.jpg" width="120" height="94" alt="Radim ?eh??ek" class="avatar avatar-120 wp-user-avatar wp-user-avatar-120 alignnone photo"></span> 
           <span class="bypostauthor">Post<br>Author</span>
          </div> 
          <article id="comment-2386" class="comment"> 
           <header class="x-comment-header"> 
            <cite class="x-comment-author"><a href="http://radimrehurek.com" rel="external nofollow" class="url">Radim ?eh??ek</a></cite>
            <div>
             <a href="https://rare-technologies.com/word2vec-tutorial/#comment-2386" class="x-comment-time"><time datetime="2016-04-02T02:10:09+00:00">2016-04-02 at 2:10 am</time></a>
            </div> 
           </header> 
           <section class="x-comment-content"> 
            <p>Hello Henry,<br> <br> the best place for such questions is the mailing list: <a href="http://radimrehurek.com/gensim/support.html" rel="nofollow">http://radimrehurek.com/gensim/support.html</a><br> <br> In this case, the problem comes from the fact the vocabulary scan is only done once. You can continue training on new sentences, but cannot add any new vocabulary. There is an ongoing work (pull request) to allow dynamic training including new vocabulary in gensim, but it’s not finished yet.<br> <br> If you have any follow up questions, please use the <a href="http://radimrehurek.com/gensim/support.html" rel="nofollow">mailing list</a>.</p> 
           </section>

I thought what I needed could be done by<br> model.build_vocab(some_sentences, keep_raw_vocab=True)<br> after model loading.</p>

   <script>

  jQuery(document).ready(function($) {

    var windowObj            = $(window);
    var body                 = $('body');
    var bodyOffsetBottom     = windowObj.scrollBottom();             // 1
    var bodyHeightAdjustment = body.height() - bodyOffsetBottom;     // 2
    var bodyHeightAdjusted   = body.height() - bodyHeightAdjustment; // 3
    var scrollTopAnchor      = $('.x-scroll-top');

    function sizingUpdate(){
      var bodyOffsetTop = windowObj.scrollTop();
      if ( bodyOffsetTop > ( bodyHeightAdjusted * 0.25 ) ) {
        scrollTopAnchor.addClass('in');
      } else {
        scrollTopAnchor.removeClass('in');
      }
    }

    windowObj.bind('scroll', sizingUpdate).resize(sizingUpdate);
    sizingUpdate();

    scrollTopAnchor.click(function(){
      $('html,body').animate({ scrollTop: 0 }, 850, 'easeInOutExpo');
      return false;
    });

  });

  </script>

	if(element.addEventListener) {

	} else if(element.attachEvent){

	}
}function maybePrefixUrlField() {
	if(this.value.trim() !== '' && this.value.indexOf('http') !== 0) {
		this.value = "http://" + this.value;
	}
}

if( testInput.type !== 'date') {

	/* add placeholder & pattern to all date fields */
	var dateFields = document.querySelectorAll('.mc4wp-form input[type="date"]');
	for(var i=0; i<dateFields.length; i++) {
		if(!dateFields[i].placeholder) {

		if(!dateFields[i].pattern) {

	}

			$height += 50;
			$height += "px";
			_nav.next().css("padding-top", $height);
			_nav.css("height", '$height');
		} else if (_cur_top < 1) {
			_nav.removeClass('top');
			_nav.removeClass('hide');
			_nav.next().css("padding-top", '');
		} else if (_top < _cur_top && _top > 300) {
      _nav.addClass('hide');
			_nav.removeClass('top');
		}
		_top = $(window).scrollTop();
	});
  
function addAnchors(){
    //loop through all your headers
    $.each($('h1, h2, h3'),function(){
        //append the text of your header to a list item in a div, linking to an anchor we will create on the next line
        var link_text = $(this).text().replace(/[^a-z0-9\s]/gi, '').split(' ').join('_').trim().toLowerCase();
        var heading_text = $(this).text();
        var link = link_text.substring(0, 30);
       if(link.length > 29){
          var parts = link.split('_');
        	var loc = parts.pop();
					var link = parts.join('_');
        }
        
        $(this).attr('id', link);
        //$(this).html(heading_text);
        $(this).prepend('<a class="anchor dashicons" href="#'+link+'"></a>');
    });
}
  addAnchors();
});    </script>   
 </body>
</html>
